   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">Father's Day</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

      <p><b>Father's Day</b> is a day of honouring fatherhood and paternal bonds, as well as the influence of fathers in society. In Catholic countries of Europe, it has been celebrated on March 19 as <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph%27s_Day" title="Saint Joseph's Day">Saint Joseph's Day</a> since the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. In America, Father's Day was founded by <a href="/wiki/Sonora_Smart_Dodd" title="Sonora Smart Dodd">Sonora Smart Dodd</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> and celebrated on the third Sunday of June for the first time in 1910. The day is held on various dates across the world and different regions maintain their own traditions of honouring fatherhood. </p>
      <p>Father's day complements similar celebrations honouring family members, such as <a href="/wiki/Mother%27s_Day" title="Mother's Day">Mother's Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siblings_Day" title="Siblings Day">Siblings Day</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grandparents_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Grandparents Day">Grandparents' Day</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>For centuries, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a> has appointed the second Sunday before Nativity as the <a href="/wiki/Nativity_Fast#Sunday_of_the_Forefathers" title="Nativity Fast">Sunday of the Forefathers</a> to commemorate the ancestors of <a href="/wiki/Christ" class="mw-redirect" title="Christ">Christ</a> according to the flesh, starting with <a href="/wiki/Adam" title="Adam">Adam</a> and emphasizing the Patriarch <a href="/wiki/Abraham" title="Abraham">Abraham</a>, to whom God said, </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p> In thy seed shall all of the nations of the earth be blessed </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        — <cite>Genesis 12:3, 22:18</cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>This feast can fall between December 11 and 17.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> This feast includes the ancestors of the <a href="/wiki/Mary,_mother_of_Jesus" title="Mary, mother of Jesus">Mary, mother of Jesus</a> and various prophets. </p>
      <p>A customary day for the celebration of fatherhood in <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> is known to date back to at least 1508. It is usually celebrated on <a href="/wiki/March_19" title="March 19">March 19</a>, as the feast day of Saint Joseph, who is referred to as the fatherly <i>Nutritor Domini</i> ("Nourisher of the Lord") in Catholicism and "the putative father of <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a>" in southern European tradition. This celebration was brought to the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> actively supported the custom of a celebration of fatherhood on St. Joseph's Day from either the last years of the <a href="/wiki/14th_century" title="14th century">14th century</a> or from the early <a href="/wiki/15th_century" title="15th century">15th century</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-natgeo_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo-6">[6]</a></sup> apparently on the initiative of the <a href="/wiki/Franciscans" title="Franciscans">Franciscans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Orthodox_Church_of_Alexandria" title="Coptic Orthodox Church of Alexandria">Coptic Orthodox Church</a>, the celebration of fatherhood is also observed on St Joseph's Day, but the Copts observe this on July 20. The Coptic celebration may date back to the fifth century.<sup id="cite_ref-natgeo_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo-6">[6]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Whether to celebrate this day worldwide or not remained a debatable topic for long. Then, in 1908, by Grace Golden Clayton proposed the day to honour those men who lost their lives in a mining accident in the US. Though it was not accepted then. But in 1909 Sonora Smart Dodd, who along with her five brothers were raised by her father alone, being inspired after attending <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mother%E2%80%99s_day&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mother’s day (page does not exist)">Mother’s day</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> in a church, convinced the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spokane_Ministerial_Association&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Spokane Ministerial Association (page does not exist)">Spokane Ministerial Association</a> to celebrate father’s day worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In addition to Father's Day, <a href="/wiki/International_Men%27s_Day" title="International Men's Day">International Men's Day</a> is celebrated in many countries on November 19 in honor of men including boys.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dates">Dates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Dates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <div class="reflist reflist-columns references-column-width reflist-lower-roman" style="column-width: 15em;"> 
       <ol class="references"> 
        <li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Officially, as the name suggests, the holiday celebrates people who are serving or were serving the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Armed_Forces" title="Russian Armed Forces">Russian Armed Forces</a> (both men and women). But the congratulations are traditionally, nationally accepted by all fathers, other adult men and male children as well.</span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As with Russia, the celebration is officially for people who served or are serving in the <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_Armed_Forces" title="Mongolian Armed Forces">Mongolian Armed Forces</a>, but the congratulations are for all fathers and all other adult men and male children as well.</span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Taiwan only. Though Father's Day on August 8 was first celebrated in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> in 1945, there is no longer an official Father's Day in <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a> since 1949.</span> </li> 
       </ol>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="African_traditions">African traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: African traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Algeria">Algeria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Algeria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, the third Sunday in June is the dedicated day to celebrate the Father's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">Egypt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Egypt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on June 21 of every year.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kenya">Kenya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Kenya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday of June and is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Morocco">Morocco</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Morocco">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, the third Sunday in June is the dedicated day to celebrate the Father's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mozambique">Mozambique</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Mozambique">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Mozambique, father's day is observed on March 19 every year.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seychelles">Seychelles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Seychelles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on June 16 and is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday of June. It is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Sudan">South Sudan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: South Sudan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In South Sudan, Father's Day is celebrated on the last Monday of August. President <a href="/wiki/Salva_Kiir_Mayardit" title="Salva Kiir Mayardit">Salva Kiir Mayardit</a> proclaimed it before August 27, 2012. First celebrated on August 27, 2012, Father's Day was not celebrated in South Sudan in 2011 (due to the country's independence).<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sudan">Sudan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sudan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, Father's Day (عيد الأب), is celebrated on the twenty-first of June.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Asian_traditions">Asian traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Asian traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the People's Republic of China, there is no official Father's Day. Some people celebrate on the third Sunday of June, according to the tradition of the United States. Father's Day is also celebrated in the <a href="/wiki/Special_administrative_regions_of_China" title="Special administrative regions of China">special administrative regions</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, it is celebrated on the third Sunday of June and is not a public holiday. In <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>, Father's Day (<i>Dia do Pai</i>) is celebrated on the third Sunday of June and is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[43]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Father's Day is observed on the third Sunday of June in India. The event is not a public holiday. The day is usually celebrated only in bigger cities like Hyderabad, Chennai, Mumbai, New Delhi, Kanpur, Bengaluru, Kolkata, Pune and others. After this day was first observed in the United States in 1908 and gradually gained popularity,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[44]</a></sup> Indian metropolitan cities, much later, followed suit by recognising this event. In India, the day is usually celebrated with children giving gifts like greeting cards, electronic gadgets, shirts, coffee mugs or books to their fathers.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-8">[8]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia">Indonesia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Indonesia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on November 12 and is not a public holiday. Father's Day in Indonesia was first declared in 2006 in <a href="/wiki/Surakarta" title="Surakarta">Surakarta</a> City Hall attended by hundreds of people from various community groups, including people from community of inter-religion communication. Because of its recent declaration, there is not very much hype about the celebration, compared to the celebration of Mother's Day on December 22.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[46]</a></sup> Google also created its doodle for Indonesia in 2019<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[47]</a></sup> and 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[48]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, Father's Day is usually celebrated as part of Family Day on <a href="/wiki/Shevat" title="Shevat">Shevat</a> 30, though some celebrate on May 1 together with Workers' Day or Labour Day.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[49]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Japan, Father's Day (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese-language text">父の日</span>, <i lang="ja-Latn" title="Japanese-language romanization">chichi no hi</i>) is celebrated on the third Sunday of June and is not a public holiday. Common presents are <a href="/wiki/Sake" title="Sake">sake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shochu" class="mw-redirect" title="Shochu">shochu</a>, fashion items, some kinds of gourmet food, sports equipment and various <a href="/wiki/Candy" title="Candy">sweets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Kazakhstan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Since 2012, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> celebrates <a href="/wiki/Defender_of_the_Fatherland_Day_(Kazakhstan)" title="Defender of the Fatherland Day (Kazakhstan)">Defender of the Fatherland Day</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kazakh_language" title="Kazakh language">Kazakh</a>: <span lang="kk">Отан Қорғаушы күні</span>) to commemorate the foundation of the armed forces. It is also called Army Day and it is celebrated on May 7. Kazakh society perceives it as ‘a men’s day’ and honouring men so it is vaguely a celebration of fathers.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Korea">Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, Parents' day (<a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>: <span lang="ko">어버이날</span>) is celebrated on May 8 and is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup> Setting Parents' Day as a national holiday and holding a pan-national event is intended to inherit and develop traditional ethical standards such as filial piety and senior citizens' ideology. Regardless of age or gender, this day is also an opportunity to reaffirm that traditional filial piety is a crucial norm and cultural value in modern society. The ceremony to mark Parents' Day as an anniversary and put on carnations stems from a Christian culture. As Western religions and cultures entered, this holiday, which was introduced together, became the most traditional holiday combined with Confucian filial piety in the process of establishing itself. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">Malaysia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Malaysia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, Father's Day falls on the third Sunday of June.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mongolia">Mongolia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Mongolia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Mongolian Men's Association began the celebration of Father's Day on 8 August since 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nepal">Nepal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Nepal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gokarna_Aunsi" title="Gokarna Aunsi">Gokarna Aunsi</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Newar population (natives of Kathmandu valley) in Nepal honors fathers on the day of <i>kusa aunsi</i>, which occurs in late August or early September, depending on the year, since it depends on the <a href="/wiki/Lunar_calendar" title="Lunar calendar">lunar calendar</a>. The Western-inspired celebration of Father's Day that was imported into the country is always celebrated on the same day as <i>Gokarna Aunsi</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-58">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The rest of the population has also begun to celebrate the <i>Gokarna Aunsi</i> day<sup id="cite_ref-:1_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-58">[55]</a></sup> It is commonly known as <i>Abu ya Khwa Swoyegu</i> in <a href="/wiki/Nepal_Bhasa" class="mw-redirect" title="Nepal Bhasa">Nepal Bhasa</a> or <i lang="ne" title="Nepali-language text">Buwaako mukh herne din</i> (<a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">Nepali</a>: <span lang="ne">बुवाको मुख हेर्ने दिन</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a> </small>'day for looking at father's face').<sup id="cite_ref-nepal_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nepal-35">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nepal3_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nepal3-59">[56]</a></sup> On the new moon day (<i><a href="/wiki/Amavasya" title="Amavasya">Amavasya</a></i>), it is traditional to pay respect to one's deceased father; Hindus go to the <a href="/wiki/Shiva" title="Shiva">Shiva</a> temple of <a href="/wiki/Gokarneswor_Mahadev" class="mw-redirect" title="Gokarneswor Mahadev">Gokarneswor Mahadev</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Gokarna,_Nepal" class="mw-redirect" title="Gokarna, Nepal">Gokarna</a>, a suburb of <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu" title="Kathmandu">Kathmandu</a><sup id="cite_ref-MayhewBindloss2009_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MayhewBindloss2009-60">[57]</a></sup> while Buddhists go to Jan Bahal (Seto Machhendranath or white Tara) temple in Kathmandu. </p>
      <p>Traditionally, in the <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu_Valley" title="Kathmandu Valley">Kathmandu Valley</a>, the south-western corner is reserved for women and women-related rituals, and the north-eastern is for men and men-related rituals. The worship place for <i><a href="/wiki/Mata_Tirtha_Aunsi" class="mw-redirect" title="Mata Tirtha Aunsi">Mata Tirtha Aunsi</a></i> ('Mother Pilgrimage New Moon') is located in Mata Tirtha in the south-western half of the valley, while the worship place for Gokarna Aunsi is located in the north-eastern half. This division is reflected in many aspects of the life in the Kathmandu Valley.<sup id="cite_ref-HeestermanHoek1992_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HeestermanHoek1992-61">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday of June. The <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_WPF" class="mw-redirect" title="Rutgers WPF">Rutgers WPF</a> launched a campaign titled 'Greening Pakistan&nbsp;– Promoting Responsible Fatherhood' on Father's Day (Sunday June 18, 2017) across Pakistan to promote active fatherhood and responsibility for the care and upbringing of children.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup> Father's Day is not a public holiday in Pakistan. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, Father's Day is officially celebrated every third Sunday of June according to a recent presidential proclamation,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[61]</a></sup> but it is not a public holiday. It is more widely observed by the public on the 3rd Sunday of June perhaps due to <a href="/wiki/American_Colonial_Period_(Philippines)" class="mw-redirect" title="American Colonial Period (Philippines)">American influence</a> and as proclaimed in 1988 by Philippine President <a href="/wiki/Corazon_Aquino" title="Corazon Aquino">Corazon Aquino</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Under Proclamation No. 58, series of 1998, issued by then Philippine President Joseph Ejercito Estrada, the first Monday of December of every year was designated as Mother's Day and Father's Day. This Proclamation expressly repealed Proclamation No. 266, series of 1988 issued by the late Pres. Corazon Cojuangco-Aquino. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singapore">Singapore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Singapore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday of June but is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sri_Lanka">Sri Lanka</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sri Lanka">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Father's Day (<a href="/wiki/Sinhala_language" title="Sinhala language">Sinhala</a>: <span lang="si" title="Sinhala-language text">පියවරුන්ගේ දිනය</span>, <i lang="si-Latn" title="Sinhala-language romanization">Piyawarunge dhinaya</i>; <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>: <span lang="ta" title="Tamil-language text">தந்தையர் தினம்</span>, <i lang="ta-Latn" title="Tamil-language romanization">Thanthaiyar Thinam</i>) is observed on the third Sunday of June. It is not a public holiday. Many schools hold special events to honor fathers.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taiwan">Taiwan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Taiwan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Taiwan" title="Public holidays in Taiwan">Public holidays in Taiwan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, Father's Day is not an official holiday, but is widely observed on August 8, the eighth day of the eighth month of the year. In <a href="/wiki/Standard_Chinese" title="Standard Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a>, the pronunciation of the number eight is <i>bā</i>, and the pronunciation is very similar to the character <span lang="zh">爸</span> (<i>bà</i>), which means "Pa" or "dad". The eighth day of the eighth month (<i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">bā-bā</span></i>) is a pun for dad (<span lang="zh">爸爸</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">bàba</span></i>). The Taiwanese, therefore, sometimes refer to August 8 as "Bābā Holiday" as a pun for "Dad's Holiday" (<span lang="zh">爸爸節</span>) or the more formal "Father's Day" (<span lang="zh">父親節</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[65]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thailand">Thailand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Thailand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, the birthday of the king, is set as Father's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-smiles_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smiles-34">[31]</a></sup> December 5 is the birthday of the late king <a href="/wiki/Bhumibol_Adulyadej" title="Bhumibol Adulyadej">Bhumibol Adulyadej</a> (Rama IX). Traditionally, Thais celebrate by giving their father or grandfather a <a href="/wiki/Canna_(plant)" title="Canna (plant)">canna</a> flower (<span lang="th" title="Thai-language text">ดอกพุทธรักษา</span>, <i lang="th-Latn" title="Thai-language romanization">Dok Buddha Raksa</i>), which is considered a masculine flower; however, this is not as commonly practiced today. Thai people will wear yellow on this day to show respect for the late king, because yellow is the <a href="/wiki/Color_of_the_day" class="mw-redirect" title="Color of the day">color of the day</a> for Monday, the day King Bhumibol Adulyadej was born. Thais flood the <a href="/wiki/Sanam_Luang" title="Sanam Luang">Sanam Luang</a>, a massive park in front of the palace, to watch the king give his annual speech, and often stay until the evening, when there is a national ceremony. Thais will light candles and show respect to the king by declaring their faith. This ceremony happens in almost every village in Thailand, and even overseas at Thai organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It first gained nationwide popularity in the 1980s as part of a campaign by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Prem_Tinsulanonda" title="Prem Tinsulanonda">Prem Tinsulanonda</a> to promote Thailand's royal family.<sup id="cite_ref-smiles_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smiles-34">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mother%27s_Day" title="Mother's Day">Mother's Day</a> is celebrated on the birthday of Queen <a href="/wiki/Sirikit" title="Sirikit">Sirikit</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-smiles_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smiles-34">[31]</a></sup> August 12. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday in June and is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Arab_Emirates">United Arab Emirates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: United Arab Emirates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on June 21, generally coinciding with <a href="/wiki/Midsummer" title="Midsummer">midsummer</a>'s day.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[68]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="European_traditions">European traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: European traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Roman Catholicism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the Roman Catholic tradition, Fathers are celebrated on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph%27s_Day" title="Saint Joseph's Day">Saint Joseph's Day</a> (commonly called the Feast of Saint Joseph), March 19, though in certain countries Father's Day has become a secular celebration.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[69]</a></sup> It is also common for Catholics to honor their "<a href="/wiki/Spiritual_father" class="mw-redirect" title="Spiritual father">spiritual father</a>," their <a href="/wiki/Parish_priest" class="mw-redirect" title="Parish priest">parish priest</a>, on Father's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Austria">Austria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Austria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on the second Sunday of June and it is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[71]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Belarus">Belarus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Belarus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday of June.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Belgium">Belgium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Belgium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, Father's Day (<i>Vaderdag</i>) is celebrated on the second Sunday of June or 14 June, and it is not a public holiday. Except for Antwerp, where it's celebrated on March 19.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Bulgaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on December 26 and it is not a public holiday. According to the Eastern Orthodox tradition, fathers are celebrated on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph%27s_Day" title="Saint Joseph's Day">Saint Joseph's Day</a> - one day after Christmas.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[74]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Croatia">Croatia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Croatia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, according to the Roman Catholic tradition, fathers are celebrated on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph%27s_Day" title="Saint Joseph's Day">Saint Joseph's Day</a> (<i>Dan svetog Josipa</i>), March 19. It is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[75]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Denmark">Denmark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Denmark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Constitution_Day_(Denmark)" title="Constitution Day (Denmark)">Constitution Day (Denmark)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In Denmark, Father's Day (<i>Fars dag</i>) is celebrated on June 5.<sup id="cite_ref-fars-dag-dk_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fars-dag-dk-17">[15]</a></sup> It coincides with <a href="/wiki/Constitution_Day_(Denmark)" title="Constitution Day (Denmark)">Constitution Day</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Estonia">Estonia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Estonia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, Father's day ("Isadepäev") is celebrated on the second Sunday of November. It is an established <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Estonia" title="Public holidays in Estonia">flag day</a> and a national holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finland">Finland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Finland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, Father's Day (<a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a>: <i lang="fi">Isänpäivä</i>; <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>: <i lang="sv">Fars dag</i>) is celebrated on the second Sunday of November. It is an established <a href="/wiki/Flag_days_in_Finland" title="Flag days in Finland">flag day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> lighter manufacturer "Flaminaire" introduced the idea of father's day first in 1949 for commercial reasons. Director "Marcel Quercia" wanted to sell their lighter in France. In 1950, they introduced "la Fête des Pères", which would take place every third Sunday of June (following the American example). Their slogan «&nbsp;Nos papas nous l'ont dit, pour la fête des pères, ils désirent tous un Flaminaire&nbsp;» (Our daddies told us, for father's day, they all want a Flaminaire). In 1952, the holiday was officially decreed. A national father's day committee was set up to give a prize for fathers that deserved it most (originally, candidates were nominated by the social services of each town hall's/mayor's office); This complements "la Fête des Mères" (Mother's day) which was made official in France in 1928 and added to the calendar in Vichy in 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[78]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hiking_tour_on_father%27s_day.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Hiking_tour_on_father%27s_day.JPG/220px-Hiking_tour_on_father%27s_day.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Hiking_tour_on_father%27s_day.JPG/330px-Hiking_tour_on_father%27s_day.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Hiking_tour_on_father%27s_day.JPG/440px-Hiking_tour_on_father%27s_day.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hiking_tour_on_father%27s_day.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Hiking tour on father's day with smaller wagons.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In Germany, Father's Day (<i>Vatertag</i>) is celebrated differently from other parts of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-urge_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-urge-82">[79]</a></sup> It is always celebrated on <a href="/wiki/Ascension_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Ascension Day">Ascension Day</a> (the Thursday forty days after Easter), which is a federal holiday. Regionally, it is also called men's day, <i>Männertag</i>, or gentlemen's day, <i>Herrentag</i>. It is a tradition for groups of males (young and old but usually excluding pre-teenage boys) to do a hiking tour with one or more smaller wagons, <i><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bollerwagen" class="extiw" title="de:Bollerwagen">Bollerwagen</a></i>, pulled by manpower. In the wagons are wine or beer bottles (according to the region) and traditional regional food, <i><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hausmannskost" class="extiw" title="de:Hausmannskost">Hausmannskost</a></i>. Many men use this holiday as an opportunity to get <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_intoxication" title="Alcohol intoxication">drunk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-urge_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-urge-82">[79]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Statistical_Office_of_Germany" title="Federal Statistical Office of Germany">Federal Statistical Office of Germany</a>, alcohol-related traffic accidents multiply by three on this day.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[80]</a></sup> The tradition of Father's Day is especially prevalent in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Germany">Eastern Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-urge_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-urge-82">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>These traditions are probably rooted in <a href="/wiki/Christian_faith" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian faith">Christian</a> Ascension Day's <a href="/wiki/Procession" title="Procession">processions</a> to the farmlands, which has been celebrated since the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegel2006_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegel2006-84">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stern_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stern-85">[82]</a></sup> Men would be seated in a wooden cart and carried to the village's plaza, and the mayor would award a prize to the father who had the most children, usually a big piece of ham.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegel2006_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegel2006-84">[81]</a></sup> In the late 19th century the religious component was progressively lost, especially in urban areas such as Berlin, and groups of men organized walking excursions with beer and ham.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegel2006_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegel2006-84">[81]</a></sup> By the 20th century, alcohol consumption had become a major part of the tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegel2006_84-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegel2006-84">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[83]</a></sup> Many people will take the following Friday off at work, and some schools are closed on that Friday as well; many people then use the resulting four-day-long weekend for a short vacation. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Greece">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Baba_s%27agapo_sygapa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Athens, Syntagma Square, SYGAPA, 2004" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Baba_s%27agapo_sygapa.jpg/220px-Baba_s%27agapo_sygapa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Baba_s%27agapo_sygapa.jpg/330px-Baba_s%27agapo_sygapa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Baba_s%27agapo_sygapa.jpg/440px-Baba_s%27agapo_sygapa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Baba_s%27agapo_sygapa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A 2004 outdoor banner at <a href="/wiki/Syntagma_Square" title="Syntagma Square">Syntagma Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, with the message "Μπαμπά Σ'αγαπώ", i.e. "Daddy I love you".
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In Greece, father's day (η γιορτή του πατέρα) is officially celebrated on the third Sunday of June. The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://sos-sygapa.eu/">SYGAPA</a> association, which supports the needs of divorced fathers, raises awareness and advocates for the father's role in society, is also organising various events on the day across the country.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[84]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hungary">Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday of June and is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iceland">Iceland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Iceland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on the second Sunday of November.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[86]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Ireland, Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday of June and is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, according to the Roman Catholic tradition, Father's Day is celebrated on Saint Joseph's Day, commonly called the Feast of Saint Joseph (<i>Festa di San Giuseppe</i>), March 19. It was a public holiday until 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[88]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latvia">Latvia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Latvia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, Father's Day (Tēvu diena) is celebrated on the second Sunday of September and is not a public holiday. In Latvia people did not always celebrate this day because of the USSR's influence with its own holidays. This day in Latvia was 'officially born' in 2008 when it was celebrated and marked in the calendar for the first time on September 14 (second September Sunday) to promote the idea that man as the father must be satisfied and proud of his family and children, also, the father is important to gratitude and loving words from his family for devoted to continuous altruistic concerns. Because this day is new to the country it does not have established unique traditions, but people borrow ideas from other country's Father's Day traditions to congratulate fathers in Latvia.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lithuania">Lithuania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Lithuania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, Father's Day (<i>Tėvo diena</i>) is celebrated on the first Sunday of June and is a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[90]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malta">Malta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Malta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Malta has followed the international trend and celebrates Father’s Day on the third Sunday in June. As in the case of Mother’s Day, the introduction of Father’s Day celebrations in Malta was encouraged by <a href="/wiki/Frans_Said" title="Frans Said">Frans H Said</a> (Uncle Frans of the children’s radio programmes). The first mention of Father’s Day was in June 1977,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[91]</a></sup> and the day is now part of the local events calendar. (The Times of Malta 11 June 2017) ( Il-Mument - Maltese newspaper- 18 June 2017) </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands#Constituent_countries" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">its constituent countries</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>), Father's Day (<i>Vaderdag</i>) is celebrated on the third Sunday of June and is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[92]</a></sup> Traditionally, as on Mother's Day, fathers get breakfast in bed made by their children and families gather together and have dinner, usually at the grandparents' house. In recent years, families also started having dinner out, and as on Mother's Day, it is one of the busiest days for restaurants. At school, children handcraft presents for their fathers. Consumer goods companies have all sorts of special offers for fathers: socks, ties, electronics, suits, and men's healthcare products. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Norway">Norway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Norway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, Father's day (<i>Farsdag</i>), is celebrated on the second Sunday of November. It is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[93]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, Father's Day (<a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>: <i lang="pl">Dzień Ojca</i>) is celebrated on June 23 and is not a public holiday. <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> also created its <a href="/wiki/Doodle" title="Doodle">Doodle</a> for Father's Day 2019<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[94]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portugal">Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Father's Day (<i>Dia do Pai</i>) is celebrated on March 19 (see Roman Catholic tradition below) in Portugal. It is not a bank and public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[95]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania">Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Law instituting the Father's day celebration in Romania passed on September 29, 2009 and stated that Father's day will be celebrated annually on the second Sunday of May. First time it was celebrated on <a href="/wiki/May_9th" class="mw-redirect" title="May 9th">May 9th</a> 2010. This year it will be celebrated on <a href="/wiki/10_May" class="mw-redirect" title="10 May">10 May</a> 2021. The next dates this celebration will take place are: <a href="/wiki/8_May" class="mw-redirect" title="8 May">8 May</a> 2022, <a href="/wiki/14_May" class="mw-redirect" title="14 May">14 May</a> 2023, <a href="/wiki/12_May" class="mw-redirect" title="12 May">12 May</a> 2024, <a href="/wiki/11_May" class="mw-redirect" title="11 May">11 May</a> 2025, <a href="/wiki/10_May" class="mw-redirect" title="10 May">10 May</a> 2026, <a href="/wiki/9_May" class="mw-redirect" title="9 May">9 May</a> 2027 and <a href="/wiki/14_May" class="mw-redirect" title="14 May">14 May</a> 2028. .<sup id="cite_ref-ROMANIA_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ROMANIA-16">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Russia continues the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>'s tradition of celebrating <a href="/wiki/Defender_of_the_Fatherland_Day" title="Defender of the Fatherland Day">Defender of the Fatherland Day</a> on 23 February. It is usually called "Man's Day" and it is considered the Russian equivalent of Father's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-saunders_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saunders-99">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovakia">Slovakia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Slovakia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Slovakia, Father's Day (<a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>: <i lang="sk">deň otcov</i>) is celebrated on the third Sunday of June. It is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[97]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Father's Day (<i>El Día del Padre</i>) is observed on the feast day of Saint Joseph, which is March 19.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[98]</a></sup> It is celebrated as a public holiday in some regions of Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[99]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, Father's day (<i>Fars dag</i>), is celebrated on the second Sunday of November but is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[100]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukraine">Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Ukraine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, Father's Day (<i>Den Batka</i>) is celebrated on the third Sunday of June. It is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:A_Royal_Navy_Officer_Hugs_His_Daughter_After_Returning_from_a_Long_Deployment_on_HMS_Chiddingfold_MOD_45153053.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/A_Royal_Navy_Officer_Hugs_His_Daughter_After_Returning_from_a_Long_Deployment_on_HMS_Chiddingfold_MOD_45153053.jpg/220px-A_Royal_Navy_Officer_Hugs_His_Daughter_After_Returning_from_a_Long_Deployment_on_HMS_Chiddingfold_MOD_45153053.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/A_Royal_Navy_Officer_Hugs_His_Daughter_After_Returning_from_a_Long_Deployment_on_HMS_Chiddingfold_MOD_45153053.jpg/330px-A_Royal_Navy_Officer_Hugs_His_Daughter_After_Returning_from_a_Long_Deployment_on_HMS_Chiddingfold_MOD_45153053.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/A_Royal_Navy_Officer_Hugs_His_Daughter_After_Returning_from_a_Long_Deployment_on_HMS_Chiddingfold_MOD_45153053.jpg/440px-A_Royal_Navy_Officer_Hugs_His_Daughter_After_Returning_from_a_Long_Deployment_on_HMS_Chiddingfold_MOD_45153053.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:A_Royal_Navy_Officer_Hugs_His_Daughter_After_Returning_from_a_Long_Deployment_on_HMS_Chiddingfold_MOD_45153053.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy Officer</a> hugs his daughter after returning from a long deployment on HMS <i>Chiddingfold</i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday of June.<sup id="cite_ref-DEF_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DEF-29">[27]</a></sup> The day does not have a long tradition; <i>The English Year</i> (2006) states that it entered British popular culture "sometime after the Second World War, not without opposition".<sup id="cite_ref-Englishyear_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Englishyear-105">[102]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="North_American_traditions">North American traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: North American traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Canada, Father's Day (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Fête des Pères</i>) is celebrated on the third Sunday of June and is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[103]</a></sup> Father's Day typically involves spending time with one's father or the father figures in one's life. Small family gatherings and the giving of gifts may be part of the festivities organized for Father's Day. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Costa_Rica">Costa Rica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Costa Rica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>, the Unidad Social Cristiana party presented a bill to change the celebration of Father's Day from the third Sunday of June to March 19, the day of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph" title="Saint Joseph">Saint Joseph</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[104]</a></sup> That was to give tribute to this saint, who gave his name to the capital of the country <a href="/wiki/San_Jos%C3%A9,_Costa_Rica" title="San José, Costa Rica">San José, Costa Rica</a>, so family heads will be able to celebrate Father's Day at the same time as the <a href="/wiki/Feast_of_Saint_Joseph_the_Worker" class="mw-redirect" title="Feast of Saint Joseph the Worker">Feast of Saint Joseph the Worker</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-costa_rica_aciprensa_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-costa_rica_aciprensa-20">[18]</a></sup> The official date is still the third Sunday of June. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Haiti">Haiti</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: Haiti">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, Father's Day (<i>Fête des pères</i>) is celebrated on the last Sunday of June and is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[105]</a></sup> Fathers are recognized and celebrated on this day with cards, gifts, breakfast, lunch brunch or early Sunday dinner; whether enjoying the day at the beach or mountains, spending family time or doing favourite activities. </p>
      <p>Children exclaim "<i>bonne fête papa</i>", while everyone wishes all fathers "<i>bonne Fête des Pères</i>" (Happy Father's Day). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday of June and is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[106]</a></sup> Father's Day typically involves spending time with one's father or the father figures in one's life. Small family gatherings and the giving of gifts may be part of the festivities organized for Father's Day. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trinidad_and_Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Trinidad and Tobago">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday in June and is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[107]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Father%27s_Day_(United_States)" title="Father's Day (United States)">Father's Day (United States)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In the US, Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday of June.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[108]</a></sup> Typically, families gather to celebrate the father figures in their lives. In recent years, retailers have adapted to the holiday by promoting <a href="/wiki/Greeting_cards" class="mw-redirect" title="Greeting cards">greeting cards</a> and gifts such as electronics and tools. Schools (if in session) and other children's programs commonly have activities to make Father's Day gifts.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[109]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceanian_traditions">Oceanian traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Oceanian traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Australia, Father's Day is celebrated on the first Sunday of September, which is the first Sunday of spring in Australia. Most families present fathers with gifts and cards, and share a meal. It is recognised as a national holiday, however it is not considered a public holiday. </p>
      <p>YMCA <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a> continues the tradition of honouring the role fathers and father figures play in parenting through the annual awarding of Local Community Father of the Year in 32 municipalities in Victoria. The Father's Day Council of Victoria annually recognises fathers in the Father of the Year Award.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[110]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, Fathers' Day is celebrated on the first Sunday of September and it is not a public holiday. Fathers' Day was first observed at <a href="/wiki/St_Matthew%27s,_Auckland" title="St Matthew's, Auckland">St Matthew's Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a> on 14 July 1929<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[111]</a></sup> and first appeared in commercial advertising the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[112]</a></sup> By 1931 other churches had adopted the day and in 1935 much of Australia moved to mark the day at the beginning of September.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[113]</a></sup> New Zealand followed this, with a <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a> advert in 1937<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[114]</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">Christchurch</a> Salvation Army service in 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[115]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Samoa">Samoa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=74" title="Edit section: Samoa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Samoa, Father's Day is celebrated on the second Sunday in August, and is a recognized national holiday on the Monday following. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fiji">Fiji</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: Fiji">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Fiji, Fathers Day is celebrated in September. Commercial fathers Sunday is usually on the first Sunday and then the Methodist fathers day is usually celebrated on the second Sunday. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="South_American_traditions">South American traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: South American traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Argentina">Argentina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Argentina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Father's Day in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> is celebrated on the third Sunday of June. </p>
      <p>Attempts have been made to change the date to August 24, to commemorate the day on which the "Father of the Nation", <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn" title="José de San Martín">José de San Martín</a>. became a father.<sup id="cite_ref-diariocritico_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diariocritico-18">[16]</a></sup> In 1953, the proposal to celebrate Father's Day in all educational establishments on August 24, in honor of José de San Martín, was raised to the General Direction of Schools of <a href="/wiki/Mendoza_Province" title="Mendoza Province">Mendoza Province</a>. The day was celebrated for the first time in 1958, on the third Sunday of June, but it was not included in the school calendars due to pressure from several groups.<sup id="cite_ref-2004argentina_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2004argentina-119">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Schools in the Mendoza Province continued to celebrate Father's Day on August 24, and in 1982, the provincial governor passed a law declaring Father's Day in the province to be celebrated on that day.<sup id="cite_ref-2004argentina_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2004argentina-119">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2004, a proposal to change the date to August 24 was presented to the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Chamber_of_Deputies" title="Argentine Chamber of Deputies">Argentine Chamber of Deputies</a> as a single, unified project. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chile">Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=78" title="Edit section: Chile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> Father's Day <i>(Día del padre,</i> in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>) is celebrated one month after Mother's Day, on June 21. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=79" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> Father's Day (<i>Dia dos Pais</i>, in Portuguese) is celebrated three months after Mother's Day, on the second Sunday of August. Publicist Sylvio Bhering picked the day in honor of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joachim" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Joachim">Saint Joachim</a>, patron of fathers. While it is not an official holiday (see <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Brazil" title="Public holidays in Brazil">Public holidays in Brazil</a>), it is widely observed and typically involves spending time with and giving gifts to one's father or father figure. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colombia">Colombia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=80" title="Edit section: Colombia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday of June. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Peru">Peru</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=81" title="Edit section: Peru">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday of June and is not a public holiday. People usually give a present to their fathers and spend time with him mostly during a family meal. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezuela">Venezuela</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=82" title="Edit section: Venezuela">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, Father's Day is celebrated on the third Sunday of June and is not a public holiday. Traditionally, as on Mother's Day, families gather together and have lunch, usually at the grandparents' house. In recent years, families also started having lunch out, and as on Mother's Day, it is one of the busiest days for restaurants. At school, children handcraft their present for their fathers. Consumer goods companies have all sorts of special offers for fathers: electronics, suits, and men's healthcare products. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=83" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

             <li><b><a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Adha" title="Eid al-Adha">Eid al-Adha</a></b> (Dhu al-Hijjah 10)</li>
            </ul> 
           </div></td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2">
           <div>
            <b>Bold</b> indicates major holidays commonly celebrated in Algeria, which often represent the major celebrations of the month.

          <td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2" style="font-size:90%;">
           <div>
            Legend: 
            <p>(federal) = federal holidays, (abbreviation) = state/territorial holidays, (religious) = religious holidays, (cultural) = holiday related to a specific <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census" title="Race and ethnicity in the United States Census">racial/ethnic group</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sexual_minority" title="Sexual minority">sexual minority</a>, (week) = week-long holidays, (month) = month-long holidays, (36) = <a href="/wiki/Title_36_of_the_United_States_Code" title="Title 36 of the United States Code">Title 36 Observances and Ceremonies</a><br> <b>Bold</b> indicates major holidays commonly celebrated in the United States, which often represent the major celebrations of the month.<br> </p> See also: <a href="/wiki/Lists_of_holidays" title="Lists of holidays">Lists of holidays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hallmark_holiday" title="Hallmark holiday">Hallmark holidays</a>, public holidays in the <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_the_United_States" title="Public holidays in the United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_holidays_in_New_Jersey" title="State holidays in New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_government_holidays" title="New York State government holidays">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Public holidays in Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Public holidays in the United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a>.
           </div></td>
         </tr>
        </tbody>
       </table>
      </div>
